The data plane sends to the service information about the HTTP request.\\n30: // 2. The service sends back a ``ProcessingResponse`` message that directs the data plane to either\\n31: //    stop processing, continue without it, or send it the next chunk of the message body.\\n32: // 3. If so requested, the data plane sends the server the message body in chunks, or the entire\\n33: //    body at once. In either case, the server may send back a ``ProcessingResponse`` for each\\n34: //    message it receives, or wait for a certain amount of body chunks to be received before\\n35: //    streaming back the ``ProcessingResponse`` messages.\\n36: // 4. If so requested, the data plane sends the server the HTTP trailers, and the server sends back\\n37: //    a ``ProcessingResponse``.\\n38: // 5. At this point, request processing is done, and we pick up again at step 1 when the data plane\\n39: //    receives a response from the upstream server.\\n40: // 6. At any point above, if the server closes the gRPC stream cleanly, then the data plane\\n41: //    proceeds without consulting the server.\\n42: // 7. At any point above, if the server closes the gRPC stream with an error, then the data plane\\n43: //    returns a ``500`` error to the client, unless the filter was configured to ignore errors.\\n44: //\\n45: // In other words, the process is a request/response conversation, but using a gRPC stream to make\\n46: // it easier for the server to maintain state.\\n47: service ExternalProcessor {\\n48:   // This begins the bidirectional stream that the data plane will use to\\n49:   // give the server control over what the filter does. The actual\\n50:   // protocol is described by the ``ProcessingRequest`` and ``ProcessingResponse``\\n51:   // messages below.\\n52:   rpc Process(stream ProcessingRequest) returns (stream ProcessingResponse) {\\n53:   }\\n54: }\\n55: \\n56: // This message specifies the filter protocol configurations which will be sent to the ext_proc\\n57: // server in a :ref:`ProcessingRequest <envoy_v3_api_msg_service.ext_proc.v3.ProcessingRequest>`.\\n58: // If the server does not support these protocol configurations, it may choose to close the gRPC\\n59: // stream. If the server supports these protocol configurations, it should respond based on the\\n60: // API specifications.\\n61: message ProtocolConfiguration {\\n62:   // Specifies the filter configuration\\n63:   // :ref:`request_body_mode <envoy_v3_api_field_extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3.ProcessingMode.request_body_mode>`.\\n64:   envoy.extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3.ProcessingMode.BodySendMode request_body_mode = 1\\n65:       [(validate.rules).enum = {defined_only: true}];\\n66: \\n67:   // Specifies the filter configuration\\n68:   // :ref:`response_body_mode <envoy_v3_api_field_extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3.ProcessingMode.response_body_mode>`.\\n69:   envoy.extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3.ProcessingMode.BodySendMode response_body_mode = 2\\n70:       [(validate.rules).enum = {defined_only: true}];\\n71: \\n72:   // Specifies the filter configuration\\n73:   // :ref:`send_body_without_waiting_for_header_response <envoy_v3_api_field_extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3.ExternalProcessor.send_body_without_waiting_for_header_response>`.\\n74:   // If the client is waiting for a header response from the server, setting to ``true`` means the\\n75:   // client will send the body to the server as it arrives. Setting to ``false`` means the client\\n76:   // will buffer the arrived data and not send it to the server immediately.\\n77:   bool send_body_without_waiting_for_header_response = 3;\\n78: }\\n79: \\n80: // This represents the different types of messages that the data plane can send\\n81: // to an external processing server.\\n82: // [#next-free-field: 12]\\n83: message ProcessingRequest {\\n84:   reserved 1;\\n85: \\n86:   reserved \\\"async_mode\\\";\\n87: \\n88:   // Each request message will include one of the following sub-messages. Which\\n89:   // ones are set for a particular HTTP request/response depend on the\\n90:   // processing mode.\\n91:   oneof request {\\n92:     option (validate.required) = true;\\n93: \\n94:     // Information about the HTTP request headers, as well as peer info and additional\\n95:     // properties. Unless ``observability_mode`` is ``true``, the server must send back a\\n96:     // ``HeaderResponse`` message, an ``ImmediateResponse`` message, or close the stream.\\n97:     HttpHeaders request_headers = 2;\\n98: \\n99:     // Information about the HTTP response headers, as well as peer info and additional\\n100:     // properties. Unless ``observability_mode`` is ``true``, the server must send back a\\n101:     // ``HeaderResponse`` message or close the stream.\\n102:     HttpHeaders response_headers = 3;\\n103: \\n104:     // A chunk of the HTTP request body. Unless ``observability_mode`` is ``true``, the server must\\n105:     // send back a ``BodyResponse`` message, an ``ImmediateResponse`` message, or close the stream.\\n106:     HttpBody request_body = 4;\\n107: \\n108:     // A chunk of the HTTP response body. Unless ``observability_mode`` is ``true``, the server must\\n109:     // send back a ``BodyResponse`` message or close the stream.\\n110:     HttpBody response_body = 5;\\n111: \\n112:     // The HTTP trailers for the request path. Unless ``observability_mode`` is ``true``, the server\\n120:     // must send back a ``TrailerResponse`` message or close the stream.\\n121:     //\\n122:     // This message is only sent if the trailers processing mode is set to ``SEND`` and\\n123:     // the original upstream response has trailers.\\n124:     HttpTrailers response_trailers = 7;\\n125:   }\\n126: \\n127:   // Dynamic metadata associated with the request.\\n128:   config.core.v3.Metadata metadata_context = 8;\\n129: \\n130:   // The values of properties selected by the ``request_attributes``\\n131:   // or ``response_attributes`` list in the configuration. Each entry\\n132:   // in the list is populated from the standard\\n133:   // :ref:`attributes <arch_overview_attributes>` supported in the data plane.\\n134:   map<string, google.protobuf.Struct> attributes = 9;\\n135: \\n136:   // Specifies whether the filter that sent this request is running in\\n137:   // :ref:`observability_mode <envoy_v3_api_field_extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3.ExternalProcessor.observability_mode>`.\\n138:   //\\n139:   // * A value of ``false`` indicates that the server must respond to this message by either\\n140:   //   sending back a matching ``ProcessingResponse`` message, or by closing the stream.\\n141:   // * A value of ``true`` indicates that the server should not respond to this message, as any\\n142:   //   responses will be ignored. However, it may still close the stream to indicate that no more\\n143:   //   messages are needed.\\n144:   //\\n145:   // Defaults to ``false``.\\n146:   bool observability_mode = 10;\\n147: \\n148:   // Specify the filter protocol configurations to be sent to the server.\\n149:   // ``protocol_config`` is only encoded in the first ``ProcessingRequest`` message from the client to the server.\\n150:   ProtocolConfiguration protocol_config = 11;\\n151: }\\n152: \\n153: // This represents the different types of messages the server may send back to the data plane\\n154: // when the ``observability_mode`` field in the received ``ProcessingRequest`` is set to ``false``.\\n155: //\\n156: // * If the corresponding ``BodySendMode`` in the\\n157: //   :ref:`processing_mode <envoy_v3_api_field_extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3.ExternalProcessor.processing_mode>`\\n158: //   is not set to ``FULL_DUPLEX_STREAMED``, then for every received ``ProcessingRequest``,\\n159: //   the server must send back exactly one ``ProcessingResponse`` message.\\n160: // * If it is set to ``FULL_DUPLEX_STREAMED``, the server must follow the API defined\\n161: //   for this mode to send the ``ProcessingResponse`` messages.\\n162: // [#next-free-field: 13]\\n163: message ProcessingResponse {\\n164:   // The response type that is sent by the server.\\n165:   oneof response {\\n166:     // If specified, attempt to create a locally generated response, send it\\n193:     // downstream, and stop processing additional filters and ignore any\\n194:     // additional messages received This metadata will be placed in the namespace(s) specified by the top-level\\n220:   // field name(s) of the struct.\\n221:   google.protobuf.Struct dynamic_metadata = 8;\\n222: \\n223:   // Override how parts of the HTTP request and response are processed for the duration of this\\n224:   // particular request/response only. Servers may use this to intelligently control how requests\\n225:   // are processed based on the headers and other metadata that they see.\\n226:   //\\n227:   // This field is only applicable when servers are responding to the header requests. If it is set\\n228:   // in the response to the body or trailer requests, it will be ignored by the data plane.\\n229:   // It is also ignored by the data plane when the ext_proc filter config\\n230:   // :ref:`allow_mode_override <envoy_v3_api_field_extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3.ExternalProcessor.allow_mode_override>`\\n231:   // is set to ``false``, or\\n232:   // :ref:`send_body_without_waiting_for_header_response <envoy_v3_api_field_extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3.ExternalProcessor.send_body_without_waiting_for_header_response>`\\n233:   // is set to ``true``.\\n234:   envoy.extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3.ProcessingMode mode_override = 9;\\n235: \\n236:   // [#not-implemented-hide:]\\n237:   // Used only in ``FULL_DUPLEX_STREAMED`` and ``GRPC`` body send modes.\\n238:   // Instructs the data plane to stop sending body data and to send a\\n239:   // half-close on the ext_proc stream. The ext_proc server should then echo\\n240:   // back all subsequent body contents as-is until it sees the client's\\n241:   // half-close, at which point the ext_proc server can terminate the stream\\n242:   // with an OK status. This provides a safe way for the ext_proc server\\n243:   // to indicate that it does not need to see the rest of the stream;\\n244:   // without this, the ext_proc server could not terminate the stream\\n245:   // early, because it would wind up dropping any body contents that the\\n246:   // client had already sent before it saw the ext_proc stream termination.\\n247:   bool request_drain = 12;\\n248: \\n249:   // When the ext_proc server receives a request message and needs more time to process it, it\\n250:   // sends back a ``ProcessingResponse`` message with a new timeout value. When the data plane\\n251:   // receives this response message, it ignores other fields in the response, stops the original\\n252:   // timer (which has the timeout value specified in\\n253:   // :ref:`message_timeout <envoy_v3_api_field_extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3.ExternalProcessor.message_timeout>`),\\n254:   // and starts a new timer with this ``override_message_timeout`` value while keeping the data\\n255:   // plane ext_proc filter state machine intact.\\n256:   //\\n257:   // The value must be >= 1ms and <=\\n258:   // :ref:`max_message_timeout <envoy_v3_api_field_extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3.ExternalProcessor.max_message_timeout>`.\\n259:   // Such a message can be sent at most once in a particular data plane ext_proc filter processing\\n260:   // state. To enable this API, ``max_message_timeout`` must be set to a value >= 1ms.\\n261:   google.protobuf.Duration override_message_timeout = 10;\\n262: }\\n263: \\n264: // The following are messages that are sent to the server.\\n265: \\n266: // This message is sent to the external server when the HTTP request and response headers\\n267: // are first received.\\n268: message HttpHeaders {\\n269:   // The HTTP request headers. If a response has already started, then\\n424: // this will either ship the reply directly to the downstream codec, or reset the stream.\\n425: // [#next-free-field: 6]\\n426: message ImmediateResponse {\\n427:   // The response code to return.\\n428:   type.v3.HttpStatus status = 1 [(validate.rules).message = {required: true}];\\n429: \\n430:   // Apply changes to the default headers, which will include ``content-type``.\\n431:   HeaderMutation headers = 2;\\n432: \\n433:   // The message body to return with the response which is sent using the\\n434:   // ``text/plain`` content type, or encoded in the ``grpc-message`` header.\\n435:   bytes body = 3;\\n436: \\n437:   // If set, then include a gRPC status trailer.\\n438:   GrpcStatus grpc_status = 4;\\n439: \\n440:   // A string detailing why this local reply was sent, which may be included\\n441:   // in log and debug output (e.g., this populates the ``%RESPONSE_CODE_DETAILS%``\\n442:   // command operator field for use in access logging).\\n443:   string details = 5;\\n444: }\\n445: \\n446: // This message specifies a gRPC status for an ``ImmediateResponse`` message.\\n447: message GrpcStatus {\\n448:   // The actual gRPC status.\\n449:   uint32 status = 1;\\n450: }\\n451: \\n452: // Change HTTP headers or trailers by appending, replacing, or removing\\n453: // headers.\\n454: message HeaderMutation {\\n455:   // Add or replace HTTP headers. syntax = \\\"proto3\\\";\\n2: \\n3: package envoy.service.ext_proc.v3;\\n4: \\n5: import \\\"envoy/config/core/v3/base.proto\\\";\\n6: import \\\"envoy/extensions/filters/http/ext_proc/v3/processing_mode.proto\\\";\\n7: import \\\"envoy/type/v3/http_status.proto\\\";\\n8: \\n9: import \\\"google/protobuf/duration.proto\\\";\\n10: import \\\"google/protobuf/struct.proto\\\";\\n11: \\n12: import \\\"xds/annotations/v3/status.proto\\\";\\n13: \\n14: import \\\"envoy/annotations/deprecation.proto\\\";\\n15: import \\\"udpa/annotations/status.proto\\\";\\n16: import \\\"validate/validate.proto\\\";\\n17: \\n18: option java_package = \\\"io.envoyproxy.envoy.service.ext_proc.v3\\\";\\n19: option java_outer_classname = \\\"ExternalProcessorProto\\\";\\n20: option java_multiple_files = true;\\n21: option go_package = \\\"github.com/envoyproxy/go-control-plane/envoy/service/ext_proc/v3;ext_procv3\\\";\\n22: option (udpa.annotations.file_status).package_version_status = ACTIVE;\\n23: \\n24: // [#protodoc-title: External processing service]\\n25: \\n26: // A service that can access and modify HTTP requests and responses as part of a filter chain.\\n27: // The overall external processing protocol works like this:\\n28: //\\n29: // 1. The data plane sends to the service information about the HTTP request.\\n30: // 2. The service sends back a ``ProcessingResponse`` message that directs the data plane to either\\n31: //    stop processing, continue without it, or send it the next chunk of the message body.\\n32: // 3. If so requested, the data plane sends the server the message body in chunks, or the entire\\n33: //    body at once. In either case, the server may send back a ``ProcessingResponse`` for each\\n34: //    message it receives, or wait for a certain amount of body chunks to be received before\\n35: //    streaming back the ``ProcessingResponse`` messages.\\n36: // 4. If so requested, the data plane sends the server the HTTP trailers, and the server sends back\\n37: //    a ``ProcessingResponse``.\\n38: // 5. At this point, request processing is done, and we pick up again at step 1 when the data plane\\n39: //    receives a response from the upstream server.\\n40: // 6. At any point above, if the server closes the gRPC stream cleanly, then the data plane\\n41: //    proceeds without consulting the server.\\n42: // 7. At any point above, if the server closes the gRPC stream with an error, then the data plane\\n43: //    returns a ``500`` error to the client, unless the filter was configured to ignore errors.\\n44: //\\n45: // In other words, the process is a request/response conversation, but using a gRPC stream to make\\n46: // it easier for the server to maintain state.\\n47: service ExternalProcessor {\\n48:   // This begins the bidirectional stream that the data plane will use to\\n49:   // give the server control over what the filter does. The ext_proc server should then echo\\n240:   // back all subsequent body contents as-is until it sees the client's\\n241:   // half-close, at which point the ext_proc server can terminate the stream\\n242:   // with an OK status. To enable this API, ``max_message_timeout`` must be set to a value >= 1ms.\\n261:   google.protobuf.Duration override_message_timeout = 10;\\n262: }\\n263: \\n264: // The following are messages that are sent to the server.\\n265: \\n266: // This message is sent to the external server when the HTTP request and response headers\\n267: // are first received.\\n268: message HttpHeaders {\\n269:   // The HTTP request headers. \"google/protobuf/struct.proto\";\n11: \n12: import \"xds/annotations/v3/status.proto\";\n13: \n14: import \"envoy/annotations/deprecation.proto\";\n15: import \"udpa/annotations/status.proto\";\n16: import \"validate/validate.proto\";\n17: \n18: option java_package = \"io.envoyproxy.envoy.service.ext_proc.v3\";\n19: option java_outer_classname = \"ExternalProcessorProto\";\n20: option = ACTIVE;\n23: \n24: // [#protodoc-title: External processing service]\n25: \n26: // A service that can access and modify HTTP requests and responses as part of a filter chain.\n27: // The overall external processing protocol works like this:\n28: //\n29: // 1. The data plane sends to the service information about the HTTP request.\n30: // 2. The service sends back a ``ProcessingResponse`` message that directs the data plane to either\n31: //    stop processing, continue without it, or send it the next chunk of the message body.\n32: // 3. If so requested, the data plane sends the server the message body in chunks, or the entire\n33: //    body at once. In either case, the server may send back a ``ProcessingResponse`` for each\n34: //    message it receives, or wait for a certain amount of body chunks to be received before\n35: //    streaming back the ``ProcessingResponse`` messages.\n36: // 4. If so requested, the data plane sends the server the HTTP trailers, and the server sends back\n37: //    a ``ProcessingResponse``.\n38: // 5. At this point, request processing is done, and we pick up again at step 1 when the data plane\n39: //    receives a response from the upstream server.\n40: // 6. At any point above, if the server closes the gRPC stream cleanly, then the data plane\n41: //    proceeds without consulting the server.\n42: // 7. At any point above, if the server closes the gRPC stream with an error, then the data plane\n43: //    returns a ``500`` error to the client, unless the filter was configured to ignore errors.\n44: //\n45: // In other words, the process is a request/response conversation, but using a gRPC stream to make\n46: // it easier for the server to maintain state.\n47: service ExternalProcessor {\n48:   // This begins the bidirectional stream that the data plane will use to\n49:   // give the server control over what the filter does. The actual\n50:   // protocol is described by the ``ProcessingRequest`` and ``ProcessingResponse``\n51:   // messages below.\n52:   rpc Process(stream ProcessingRequest) returns (stream ProcessingResponse) {\n53:   }\n54: }\n55: \n56: // This message specifies the filter protocol configurations which will be sent to the ext_proc\n57: // server in a :ref:`ProcessingRequest <envoy_v3_api_msg_service.ext_proc.v3.ProcessingRequest>`.\n58: // If the server does not support these protocol configurations, it may choose to close the gRPC\n59: // stream. If the server supports these protocol configurations, it should respond based on the\n60: // API specifications.\n61: message ProtocolConfiguration {\n62:   // Specifies the filter configuration\n63:   // :ref:`request_body_mode <envoy_v3_api_field_extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3.ProcessingMode.request_body_mode>`.\n64:   envoy.extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3.ProcessingMode.BodySendMode request_body_mode = 1\n65:       [(validate.rules).enum = {defined_only: true}];\n66: \n67:   // Specifies the filter configuration\n68:   // :ref:`response_body_mode <envoy_v3_api_field_extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3.ProcessingMode.response_body_mode>`.\n69:   envoy.extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3.ProcessingMode.BodySendMode response_body_mode = 2\n70:       [(validate.rules).enum = {defined_only: true}];\n71: \n72:   // Specifies the filter configuration\n73:   // :ref:`send_body_without_waiting_for_header_response <envoy_v3_api_field_extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3.ExternalProcessor.send_body_without_waiting_for_header_response>`.\n74:   // If the client is waiting for a header response from the server, setting to ``true`` means the\n75:   // client will send the body to the server as it arrives. Discovery\\n\\n### Envoy Data Plane API (envoyproxy/data-plane-api)\\n\\nThe data-plane-api repository contains gRPC service definitions for the xDS (service discovery) protocol and supporting Envoy services. These services are organized across multiple proto files and versions (v2, v2alpha, and v3).\\n\\n#### xDS Discovery Services (Core)\\nThese are the primary service discovery services used by Envoy and other xDS clients:\\n\\n1. **ClusterDiscoveryService (CDS)** - Defined in envoy/service/cluster/v3/cds.proto and envoy/api/v2/cds.proto. Provides cluster configuration discovery.\\n\\n2. **EndpointDiscoveryService (EDS)** - Defined in envoy/service/endpoint/v3/eds.proto and envoy/api/v2/eds.proto. Provides endpoint/load assignment discovery.\\n\\n3. **ListenerDiscoveryService (LDS)** - Defined in envoy/service/listener/v3/lds.proto and envoy/api/v2/lds.proto. Provides listener configuration discovery.\\n\\n4. **RouteDiscoveryService (RDS)** - Defined in envoy/service/route/v3/rds.proto and envoy/api/v2/rds.proto. Provides route configuration discovery.\\n\\n5. **SecretDiscoveryService (SDS)** - Defined in envoy/service/secret/v3/sds.proto and envoy/service/discovery/v2/sds.proto. Provides secret (TLS certificate) discovery.\\n\\n6. **VirtualHostDiscoveryService (VHDS)** - Defined in envoy/service/route/v3/rds.proto and envoy/api/v2/rds.proto. Provides virtual host configuration discovery.\\n\\n7. **ScopedRoutesDiscoveryService (SRDS)** - Defined in envoy/service/route/v3/srds.proto and envoy/api/v2/srds.proto. Provides scoped route configuration discovery.\\n\\n8. **LocalityEndpointDiscoveryService (LEDS)** - Defined in envoy/service/endpoint/v3/leds.proto. Provides locality-specific endpoint discovery.\\n\\n9. **RuntimeDiscoveryService (RTDS)** - Defined in envoy/service/runtime/v3/rtds.proto and envoy/service/discovery/v2/rtds.proto. Provides runtime configuration discovery.\\n\\n10. **AggregatedDiscoveryService (ADS)** - Defined in envoy/service/discovery/v3/ads.proto and envoy/service/discovery/v2/ads.proto. Provides multiplexed access to all xDS services.\\n\\n#### Supporting Services\\nThese services provide additional functionality for Envoy:\\n\\n11. **ClientStatusDiscoveryService (CSDS)** - Defined in envoy/service/status/v3/csds.proto and envoy/service/status/v2/csds.proto. Allows clients to report their configuration status to management servers.\\n\\n12. **AccessLogService (ALS)** - Defined in envoy/service/accesslog/v3/als.proto and envoy/service/accesslog/v2/als.proto. Streams access logs to an external logging service.\\n\\n13. **MetricsService** - Defined in envoy/service/metrics/v3/metrics_service.proto and envoy/service/metrics/v2/metrics_service.proto. Streams metrics to an external metrics service.\\n\\n14. **LoadReportingService (LRS)** - Defined in envoy/service/load_stats/v3/lrs.proto and envoy/service/load_stats/v2/lrs.proto. Reports load statistics to the management server.\\n\\n15. **RateLimitService (RLS)** - Defined in envoy/service/ratelimit/v3/rls.proto and envoy/service/ratelimit/v2/rls.proto. Provides rate limiting decisions.\\n\\n16. **RateLimitQuotaService (RLQS)** - Defined in envoy/service/rate_limit_quota/v3/rlqs.proto. Manages rate limit quota allocations.\\n\\n17. **Authorization** - Defined in envoy/service/auth/v3/external_auth.proto. Provides authorization checks for incoming requests.\\n\\n18. **ExternalProcessor** - Defined in envoy/service/ext_proc/v3/external_processor.proto. Allows external processing of HTTP requests and responses.\\n\\n19. **HealthDiscoveryService (HDS)** - Defined in envoy/service/health/v3/hds.proto. Enables Envoy instances to perform health checks on behalf of the management server.\\n\\n20. **NetworkExternalProcessor** - Defined in envoy/service/network_ext_proc/v3/network_external_processor.proto. Provides external processing capabilities for L4 network traffic.\\n\\n21. **TapSinkService** - Defined in envoy/service/tap/v2alpha/tap.proto. Receives captured traffic taps from Envoy.\\n\\n### gRPC Health Checking Protocol (grpc/grpc)\\n\\nThe gRPC repository includes the standard gRPC Health Checking Protocol (grpc_health_v1):\\n\\n**Health Service** - Defined in src/proto/grpc/health/v1/health.proto. This is the standard gRPC health checking service that provides two RPC methods:\\n- Check: Performs a one-time health check for a service\\n- Watch: Streams health status changes for a service\\n\\nImplementation files for the Health service in gRPC:\\n- src/cpp/server/health/health_check_service.cc - Core implementation\\n- src/cpp/server/health/default_health_check_service.cc - Default implementation\\n\\n### Cross-Organization Usage\\n\\nThese services represent the interface between Envoy (the data plane) and management servers (xDS providers) using a common gRPC-based protocol. The Health service is used by Envoy and other gRPC services to report their operational status. Together, they form the fundamental building blocks for service mesh control planes and gRPC infrastructure.\\n\"\n}\n"},"caller":{"type":"direct"}}],"stop_reason":null,"stop_sequence":null,"usage":{"input_tokens":7,"cache_creation_input_tokens":1317,"cache_read_input_tokens":95271,"cache_creation":{"ephemeral_5m_input_tokens":0,"ephemeral_1h_input_tokens":1317},"output_tokens":1,"service_tier":"standard","inference_geo":"not_available"},"context_management":null},"parent_tool_use_id":null,"session_id":"a77a6ac0-24f0-4c03-94a5-165f1e25af78","uuid":"f5ba7a9b-a9ab-49c5-8875-41f6278c3e07"}

Provides secret (TLS certificate) discovery.\\n\\n6. **VirtualHostDiscoveryService (VHDS)** - Defined in envoy/service/route/v3/rds.proto and envoy/api/v2/rds.proto. Provides virtual host configuration discovery.\\n\\n7. **ScopedRoutesDiscoveryService (SRDS)** - Defined in envoy/service/route/v3/srds.proto and envoy/api/v2/srds.proto. Provides scoped route configuration discovery.\\n\\n8. **LocalityEndpointDiscoveryService (LEDS)** - Defined in envoy/service/endpoint/v3/leds.proto. Provides locality-specific endpoint discovery.\\n\\n9. **RuntimeDiscoveryService (RTDS)** - Defined in envoy/service/runtime/v3/rtds.proto and envoy/service/discovery/v2/rtds.proto. Provides runtime configuration discovery.\\n\\n10. **AggregatedDiscoveryService (ADS)** - Defined in envoy/service/discovery/v3/ads.proto and envoy/service/discovery/v2/ads.proto. Provides multiplexed access to all xDS services.\\n\\n#### Supporting Services\\nThese services provide additional functionality for Envoy:\\n\\n11. **ClientStatusDiscoveryService (CSDS)** - Defined in envoy/service/status/v3/csds.proto and envoy/service/status/v2/csds.proto. Allows clients to report their configuration status to management servers.\\n\\n12. **AccessLogService (ALS)** - Defined in envoy/service/accesslog/v3/als.proto and envoy/service/accesslog/v2/als.proto. Streams access logs to an external logging service.\\n\\n13. **MetricsService** - Defined in envoy/service/metrics/v3/metrics_service.proto and envoy/service/metrics/v2/metrics_service.proto. Streams metrics to an external metrics service.\\n\\n14. **LoadReportingService (LRS)** - Defined in envoy/service/load_stats/v3/lrs.proto and envoy/service/load_stats/v2/lrs.proto. Reports load statistics to the management server.\\n\\n15. **RateLimitService (RLS)** - Defined in envoy/service/ratelimit/v3/rls.proto and envoy/service/ratelimit/v2/rls.proto. Provides rate limiting decisions.\\n\\n16. **RateLimitQuotaService (RLQS)** - Defined in envoy/service/rate_limit_quota/v3/rlqs.proto. Manages rate limit quota allocations.\\n\\n17. **Authorization** - Defined in envoy/service/auth/v3/external_auth.proto. Provides authorization checks for incoming requests.\\n\\n18. **ExternalProcessor** - Defined in envoy/service/ext_proc/v3/external_processor.proto. Allows external processing of HTTP requests and responses.\\n\\n19. **HealthDiscoveryService (HDS)** - Defined in envoy/service/health/v3/hds.proto. Enables Envoy instances to perform health checks on behalf of the management server.\\n\\n20. **NetworkExternalProcessor** - Defined in envoy/service/network_ext_proc/v3/network_external_processor.proto. Provides external processing capabilities for L4 network traffic.\\n\\n21. **TapSinkService** - Defined in envoy/service/tap/v2alpha/tap.proto. Receives captured traffic taps from Envoy.\\n\\n### gRPC Health Checking Protocol (grpc/grpc)\\n\\nThe gRPC repository includes the standard gRPC Health Checking Protocol (grpc_health_v1):\\n\\n**Health Service** - Defined in src/proto/grpc/health/v1/health.proto. This is the standard gRPC health checking service that provides two RPC methods:\\n- Check: Performs a one-time health check for a service\\n- Watch: Streams health status changes for a service\\n\\nImplementation files for the Health service in gRPC:\\n- src/cpp/server/health/health_check_service.cc - Core implementation\\n- src/cpp/server/health/default_health_check_service.cc - Default implementation\\n\\n### Cross-Organization Usage\\n\\nThese services represent the interface between Envoy (the data plane) and management servers (xDS providers) using a common gRPC-based protocol. The Health service is used by Envoy and other gRPC services to report their operational status. Together, they form the fundamental building blocks for service mesh control planes and gRPC infrastructure.\\n\"\n}\n","structuredPatch":[],"originalFile":null}}
